Others</li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Demonym" title="Demonym">Demonym(s)</a></th><td>Namibian</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Namibia" numbers in Namibia">Calling code</a></th><td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%2B264" title="+264">+264</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/ISO_3166" title="ISO 3166">ISO 3166 code</a></th><td><a href="/wiki/ISO_3166-2:NA" title="ISO 3166-2:NA">NA</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Country_code_top-level_domain" title="Country code top-level domain">Internet TLD</a></th><td><a href="/wiki/.na" title=".na">.na</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Namibia</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="\'n\' in \'nigh\'">n</span><span title="/&#601;/: \'a\' in \'about\'">&#601;</span><span title="/&#712;/: primary stress follows">&#712;</span><span title="\'m\' in \'my\'">m</span><span title="/&#618;/: \'i\' in \'kit\'">&#618;</span><span title="\'b\' in \'buy\'">b</span><span title="/i/: \'y\' in \'happy\'">i</span><span title="/&#601;/: \'a\' in \'about\'">&#601;</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Namibia.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" decoding="async" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a></span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/3e/En-ca-Namibia.oga" title="En-ca-Namibia.oga">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>, <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="\'n\' in \'nigh\'">n</span><span title="/&#230;/: \'a\' in \'bad\'">&#230;</span><span title="/&#712;/: primary stress follows">&#712;</span></span>-/</a></span></span>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> officially the <b>Republic of Namibia</b>, is a country in <a href="/wiki/Southern_Africa" title="Southern Africa">southern Africa</a>. Its western border is the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>; it shares land borders with <a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">Zambia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a> to the north, <a href="/wiki/Botswana" title="Botswana">Botswana</a> to the east and <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a> to the south and east. Although <a href="/wiki/Kazungula" title="Kazungula">it does not</a> border <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a>, less than 200 metres of the <a href="/wiki/Zambezi" title="Zambezi">Zambezi River</a> (essentially a small bulge in Botswana to achieve a Botswana/Zambia micro-border) separates the two countries. Namibia gained independence from South Africa on 21 March 1990, following the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Namibian_War_of_Independence" title="Namibian War of Independence">Namibian War of Independence</a>. Its capital and largest city is <a href="/wiki/Windhoek" title="Windhoek">Windhoek</a>, and it is a member state of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> (UN), the <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Development_Community" title="Southern African Development Community">Southern African Development Community</a> (SADC), the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a> (AU), and the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>.\n</p><p>Namibia, the driest country in Sub-Saharan Africa,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> was inhabited since early times by the <a href="/wiki/San_people" title="San people">San</a>, <a href="/wiki/Damara_people" title="Damara people">Damara</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nama_people" title="Nama people">Nama peoples</a>. Around the 14th century, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Immigrating" title="Immigrating">immigrating</a> <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantu peoples</a> arrived as part of the <a href="/wiki/Bantu_expansion" title="Bantu expansion">Bantu expansion</a>. Since then, the Bantu groups, one of which is known as the <a href="/wiki/Ovambo_people" title="Ovambo people">Ovambo people</a>, have dominated the population of the country; since the late 19th century, they have constituted a majority.\n</p><p>In 1878, the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Colony" title="Cape Colony">Cape of Good Hope</a>, then a British colony, had annexed the port of <a href="/wiki/Walvis_Bay" title="Walvis Bay">Walvis Bay</a> and the offshore <a href="/wiki/Penguin_Islands" title="Penguin Islands">Penguin Islands</a>; these became an integral part of the new <a href="/wiki/Union_of_South_Africa" title="Union of South Africa">Union of South Africa</a> at its creation in 1910. In 1884 the <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German Empire</a> established rule over most of the territory as a protectorate (<i>Schutzgebiet</i>). It began to develop infrastructure and farming and maintained this German colony until 1915, when South African forces defeated its military. In 1920, after the end of <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a> mandated the country to the United Kingdom, under administration by South Africa. It imposed its laws, including racial classifications and rules.\n</p><p>From 1948, with the <a href="/wiki/National_Party_(South_Africa)" title="National Party (South Africa)">National Party</a> elected to power, South Africa applied <a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">apartheid</a> also to what was then known as <a href="/wiki/South_West_Africa" title="South West Africa">South West Africa</a>.\n</p><p>In the later 20th century, uprisings and demands for political representation by native African political activists seeking independence resulted in the UN assuming direct responsibility over the territory in 1966, but South Africa maintained <i>de facto</i> rule. In 1973 the UN recognised the South West Africa People\'s Organisation (<a href="/wiki/SWAPO" title="SWAPO">SWAPO</a>) as the official representative of the Namibian people; the party is dominated by the Ovambo, who are a large plurality in the territory. Following continued guerrilla warfare, South Africa installed an interim administration in Namibia in 1985. Namibia obtained full independence from South Africa in 1990. However, <a href="/wiki/Walvis_Bay" title="Walvis Bay">Walvis Bay</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Penguin_Islands" title="Penguin Islands">Penguin Islands</a> remained under South African control until 1994.\n</p><p>Namibia has a population of 2.6&#160;million people and a stable <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">multi-party</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parliamentary_democracy" title="Parliamentary democracy">parliamentary democracy</a>. Agriculture, <a href="/wiki/Herding" title="Herding">herding</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Namibia" title="Tourism in Namibia">tourism</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mineral_industry_of_Namibia" title="Mineral industry of Namibia">mining industry</a>&#160;&#8211; including mining for gem diamonds, <a href="/wiki/Uranium_mining" title="Uranium mining">uranium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gold_mining" title="Gold mining">gold</a>, <a href="/wiki/Silver_mining" title="Silver mining">silver</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Base_metal" title="Base metal">base metals</a>&#160;&#8211; form the basis of its <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Namibia" title="Economy of Namibia">economy</a>. The large, arid <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Namib_Desert" title="Namib Desert">Namib Desert</a> has resulted in Namibia being overall one of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_territories_by_population_density" title="List of countries and territories by population density">least densely populated</a> countries in the world.\n</p>\n<div class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30"><a href="#Health"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Health</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-32"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-33"><a href="#Footnotes"><span class="tocnumber">12.1</span> <span class="toctext">Footnotes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-34"><a href="#Bibliography"><span class="tocnumber">12.2</span> <span class="toctext">Bibliography</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-35"><a href="#General_references"><span class="tocnumber">12.3</span> <span class="toctext">General references</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-36"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The name of the country is derived from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Namib_Desert" title="Namib Desert">Namib Desert</a>, considered to be the oldest desert in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-at1315_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-at1315-20">[20]</a></sup> The name, <i>Namib</i> itself, is of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nama_language" title="Nama language">Nama</a> origin and means "vast place". Before its independence in 1990, the area was known first as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_South-West_Africa" title="German South-West Africa">German South-West Africa</a> (<i>Deutsch-S&#252;dwestafrika</i>), then as South-West Africa, reflecting the colonial occupation by the Germans and the South Africans (technically on behalf of the British crown reflecting South Africa\'s dominion status within the British Empire).\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Namibia" title="History of Namibia">History of Namibia</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-colonial_period">Pre-colonial period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Pre-colonial period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The dry lands of Namibia have been inhabited since early times by San, Damara, and Nama. Around the 14th century, immigrating <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bantu_people" title="Bantu people">Bantu people</a> began to arrive during the <a href="/wiki/Bantu_expansion" title="Bantu expansion">Bantu expansion</a> from central Africa.\n</p><p>From the late 18th century onward, <a href="/wiki/Oorlam_people" title="Oorlam people">Oorlam people</a> from Cape Colony crossed the <a href="/wiki/Orange_River" title="Orange River">Orange River</a> and moved into the area that today is southern Namibia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KDA_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-KDA-21">[21]</a></sup> Their encounters with the nomadic Nama tribes were largely peaceful. They received the missionaries accompanying the Oorlam very well,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dierks_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dierks-22">[22]</a></sup> granting them the right to use waterholes and grazing against an annual payment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVedder1997177_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVedder1997177-23">[23]</a></sup> On their way further northwards, however, the Oorlam encountered clans of the <a href="/wiki/Herero_people" title="Herero people">Herero</a> at Windhoek, <a href="/wiki/Gobabis" title="Gobabis">Gobabis</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Okahandja" title="Okahandja">Okahandja</a>, who resisted their encroachment. The Nama-Herero War broke out in 1880, with hostilities ebbing only after the <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German Empire</a> deployed troops to the contested places and cemented the status quo among the Nama, Oorlam, and Herero.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVedder1997659_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVedder1997659-24">[24]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The first Europeans to disembark and explore the region were the Portuguese navigators <a href="/wiki/Diogo_C%C3%A3o" title="Diogo C&#227;o">Diogo C&#227;o</a> in 1485 and <a href="/wiki/Bartolomeu_Dias" title="Bartolomeu Dias">Bartolomeu Dias</a> in 1486, but the Portuguese crown did not try to claim the area. Like most of interior <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan Africa</a>, Namibia was not extensively explored by Europeans until the 19th century. At that time traders and settlers came principally from Germany and Sweden. In the late 19th century, <a href="/wiki/Dorsland_Trek" title="Dorsland Trek">Dorsland Trekkers</a> crossed the area on their way from the <a href="/wiki/South_African_Republic" title="South African Republic">Transvaal</a> to <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a>. Some of them settled in Namibia instead of continuing their journey.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="German_rule">German rule</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: German rule">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/German_South_West_Africa" title="German South West Africa">German South West Africa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Herero_and_Namaqua_genocide" title="Herero and Namaqua genocide">Herero and Namaqua genocide</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kirche_denkmal_nam.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Kirche_denkmal_nam.jpg/220px-Kirche_denkmal_nam.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Kirche_denkmal_nam.jpg/330px-Kirche_denkmal_nam.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Kirche_denkmal_nam.jpg/440px-Kirche_denkmal_nam.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kirche_denkmal_nam.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>German church and monument to colonists in Windhoek, Namibia.</div></div></div>\n<p>Namibia became a German colony in 1884 under <a href="/wiki/Otto_von_Bismarck" title="Otto von Bismarck">Otto von Bismarck</a> to forestall perceived British encroachment and was known as <a href="/wiki/German_South_West_Africa" title="German South West Africa">German South West Africa</a> (<i>Deutsch-S&#252;dwestafrika</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> However, the <a href="/wiki/Palgrave_Commission" title="Palgrave Commission">Palgrave Commission</a> by the British governor in Cape Town had determined that only the natural deep-water harbor of <a href="/wiki/Walvis_Bay" title="Walvis Bay">Walvis Bay</a> was worth occupying and thus annexed it to the Cape province of British South Africa.\n</p><p>From 1904 to 1907, the <a href="/wiki/Herero_people" title="Herero people">Herero</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Nama_people" title="Nama people">Namaqua</a> <a href="/wiki/Herero_Wars" title="Herero Wars">took up arms</a> against brutal German colonialism. In calculated punitive action by the German occupiers, government officials ordered extinction of the natives in the <a href="/wiki/Herero_and_Namaqua_genocide" title="Herero and Namaqua genocide">Herero and Namaqua genocide</a> In what has been called the "first genocide of the Twentieth Century",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> the Germans systematically killed 10,000 Nama (half the population) and approximately 65,000 Herero (about 80% of the population).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Adhikari_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-Adhikari-28">[28]</a></sup> The survivors, when finally released from detention, were subjected to a policy of dispossession, deportation, forced labor, racial segregation, and discrimination in a system that in many ways anticipated the <a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">apartheid</a> established by South Africa in 1948.\n</p><p>Most Africans were confined to so-called native territories, which later under South African rule after 1949 were turned into "homelands" (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bantustans" title="Bantustans">Bantustans</a>). Indeed, some historians have speculated that the German genocide in Namibia was a model used by <a href="/wiki/Nazism" title="Nazism">Nazis</a> in <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">the Holocaust</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Madley_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Madley-29">[29]</a></sup> The memory of genocide remains relevant to ethnic identity in independent Namibia and to relations with Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> The German government formally apologized for the Namibian genocide in 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_African_mandate">South African mandate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: South African mandate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/South_West_Africa" title="South West Africa">South West Africa</a></div>\n<p>During World War I, South African troops under General <a href="/wiki/Louis_Botha" title="Louis Botha">Louis Botha</a> <a href="/wiki/South_West_Africa_campaign" title="South West Africa campaign">occupied the territory</a> and deposed the German colonial administration. The end of the war and the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles" title="Treaty of Versailles">Treaty of Versailles</a> left South Africa in possession of South West Africa as a <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations_mandate" title="League of Nations mandate">League of Nations mandate</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rajagopal_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rajagopal-32">[32]</a></sup> The mandate system was formed as a compromise between those who advocated for an Allied annexation of former German and Turkish territories, and another proposition put forward by those who wished to grant them to an international trusteeship until they could govern themselves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rajagopal_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rajagopal-32">[32]</a></sup> It permitted the South African government to administer South West Africa for an undefined period until that territory\'s inhabitants were prepared for political self-determination.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Louis_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-Louis-33">[33]</a></sup> However, South Africa interpreted the mandate as a veiled annexation and made no attempt to prepare South West Africa for future autonomy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Louis_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-Louis-33">[33]</a></sup>\n</p><p>As a result of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Conference_on_International_Organization" title="United Nations Conference on International Organization">Conference on International Organization</a> in 1945, the League of Nations was formally superseded by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> (UN) and former League mandates by a trusteeship system. Article 77 of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_Charter" title="United Nations Charter">United Nations Charter</a> stated that UN trusteeship "shall apply...to territories now held under mandate"; furthermore, it would "be a matter of subsequent agreement as to which territories in the foregoing territories will be brought under the trusteeship system and under what terms".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vandenbosch_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-Vandenbosch-34">[34]</a></sup> The UN requested all former League of Nations mandates be surrendered to its <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Trusteeship_Council" title="United Nations Trusteeship Council">Trusteeship Council</a> in anticipation of their independence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vandenbosch_34-1"><a href="#cite_note-Vandenbosch-34">[34]</a></sup> South Africa declined to do so and instead requested permission from the UN to formally annex South West Africa, for which it received considerable criticism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vandenbosch_34-2"><a href="#cite_note-Vandenbosch-34">[34]</a></sup> When the UN General Assembly rejected this proposal, South Africa dismissed its opinion as irrelevant and began solidifying control of the territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vandenbosch_34-3"><a href="#cite_note-Vandenbosch-34">[34]</a></sup> The UN responded by deferring to the <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">International Court of Justice</a> (ICJ), which held a number of discussions on the legality of South African rule between 1949 and 1966.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-First_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-First-35">[35]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Namibia_homelands_78.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1586" data-file-width="2084" decoding="async" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Namibia_homelands_78.jpeg/220px-Namibia_homelands_78.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Namibia_homelands_78.jpeg/330px-Namibia_homelands_78.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Namibia_homelands_78.jpeg/440px-Namibia_homelands_78.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Namibia_homelands_78.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map depicting the Police Zone (in tan) and tribal homelands (in red) as they existed in 1978. Self-governing tribal homelands appear as tan with red stripes.</div></div></div>\n<p>South Africa began imposing <i><a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">apartheid</a>,</i> its codified system of racial segregation and discrimination, on South West Africa during the late 1940s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Crawford1_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-Crawford1-36">[36]</a></sup> Black South West Africans were subject to <a href="/wiki/Pass_laws" title="Pass laws">pass laws</a>, curfews, and a host of draconian residential regulations that heavily restricted their movement. Development was concentrated in the region of the country immediately adjacent to South Africa, formally denoted as the "Police Zone", where most of the German colonial era settlements and mines were also located. Outside the Police Zone, indigenous peoples were restricted to theoretically self-governing <a href="/wiki/Bantustan" title="Bantustan">tribal homelands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Devils_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Devils-37">[37]</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the late 1950s and early 1960s, pressure for global decolonisation and national self-determination began mounting on the African continent; these factors had a radical impact on South West African nationalism. Early nationalist organisations such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_West_African_National_Union" title="South West African National Union">South West African National Union</a> (SWANU) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_West_African_People%27s_Organisation" title="South West African People\'s Organisation">South West African People\'s Organisation</a> (SWAPO) made determined attempts to establish indigenous political structures for an independent South West Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M&#252;ller_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-M&#252;ller-38">[38]</a></sup> In 1966, following the ICJ\'s controversial ruling that it had no legal standing to consider the question of South African rule, SWAPO launched an armed insurgency which escalated into part of a wider regional conflict known as the <a href="/wiki/South_African_Border_War" title="South African Border War">South African Border War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Caprivi_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-Caprivi-39">[39]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence">Independence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Independence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>As SWAPO\'s insurgency intensified, South Africa\'s case for annexation in the international community continued to decline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dobell_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dobell-40">[40]</a></sup> The UN declared that South Africa had failed in its obligations to ensure the moral and material well-being of the indigenous inhabitants of South West Africa, and had thus disavowed its own mandate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yusuf_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-Yusuf-41">[41]</a></sup> On 12 June 1968, the UN General Assembly adopted a resolution which proclaimed that, in accordance with the desires of its people, South West Africa be renamed <i>Namibia</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yusuf_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-Yusuf-41">[41]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_269" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 269">United Nations Security Council Resolution 269</a>, adopted in August 1969, declared South Africa\'s continued occupation of Namibia illegal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yusuf_41-2"><a href="#cite_note-Yusuf-41">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MAA_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-MAA-42">[42]</a></sup> In recognition of this landmark decision, SWAPO\'s armed wing was renamed the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Liberation_Army_of_Namibia" title="People\'s Liberation Army of Namibia">People\'s Liberation Army of Namibia</a> (PLAN).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Camp_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-Camp-43">[43]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Namibia became one of several flashpoints for <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> proxy conflicts in southern Africa during the latter years of the PLAN insurgency.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hughes_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hughes-44">[44]</a></sup> The insurgents sought out weapons and sent recruits to the Soviet Union for military training.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Betram_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-Betram-45">[45]</a></sup> SWAPO\'s political leadership, dependent on military aid from the Soviets, Cuba, and Angola, positioned the movement within the socialist bloc by 1975.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dreyer_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dreyer-46">[46]</a></sup> This practical alliance reinforced the prevailing perspective of SWAPO as a Soviet proxy, which dominated Cold War ideology in South Africa and the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Devils_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-Devils-37">[37]</a></sup> For its part, the Soviet Union supported SWAPO partly because it viewed South Africa as a regional Western ally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shultz_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-Shultz-47">[47]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SADF-Operations_4.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="485" data-file-width="604" decoding="async" height="177" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/SADF-Operations_4.jpg/220px-SADF-Operations_4.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/SADF-Operations_4.jpg/330px-SADF-Operations_4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/SADF-Operations_4.jpg/440px-SADF-Operations_4.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SADF-Operations_4.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>South African troops patrol the border region for PLAN insurgents, 1980s.</div></div></div>\n<p>Growing war weariness and the reduction of tensions between the superpowers compelled South Africa, Angola, and Cuba to accede to the <a href="/wiki/Tripartite_Accord_(Angola)" title="Tripartite Accord (Angola)">Tripartite Accord</a>, under pressure from both the Soviet Union and the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SACP_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-SACP-48">[48]</a></sup> South Africa accepted Namibian independence in exchange for a Cuban military withdrawal from the region and an Angolan commitment to cease all aid to PLAN.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-James_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-James-49">[49]</a></sup> PLAN and South Africa adopted an informal ceasefire in August 1988, and a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Transition_Assistance_Group" title="United Nations Transition Assistance Group">United Nations Transition Assistance Group</a> (UNTAG) was formed to monitor the Namibian peace process and supervise the return of refugees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sitkowski_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sitkowski-50">[50]</a></sup> The ceasefire was broken after PLAN made a final incursion into the territory, possibly as a result of misunderstanding UNTAG\'s directives, in March 1989.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clairborne_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-Clairborne-51">[51]</a></sup> A new ceasefire was later imposed with the condition that the insurgents were to be confined to their external bases in Angola until they could be disarmed and demobilised by UNTAG.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sitkowski_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sitkowski-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Demob_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-Demob-52">[52]</a></sup>\n</p><p>By the end of the eleven month transition period, the last South African troops had been withdrawn from Namibia, all political prisoners granted amnesty, racially discriminatory legislation repealed, and 42,000 Namibian refugees returned to their homes. Just over 97% of eligible voters participated in the country\'s first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Namibian_parliamentary_election,_1989" title="Namibian parliamentary election, 1989">parliamentary elections</a> held under a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Universal_franchise" title="Universal franchise">universal franchise</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT1989_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT1989-53">[53]</a></sup> SWAPO won a plurality of seats in the <a href="/wiki/Members_of_the_Constituent_Assembly_of_Namibia" title="Members of the Constituent Assembly of Namibia">Constituent Assembly</a> with 57% of the popular vote.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT1989_53-1"><a href="#cite_note-NYT1989-53">[53]</a></sup> This gave the party 41 seats, but not a two-thirds majority which would have enabled it to draft the constitution on its own.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT1989_53-2"><a href="#cite_note-NYT1989-53">[53]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Namibian Constitution adopted in February 1990 incorporated protection for human rights, compensation for state expropriations of private property, and established an independent judiciary, legislature, and an executive presidency (the constituent assembly became the national assembly). The country officially became independent on 21 March 1990. <a href="/wiki/Sam_Nujoma" title="Sam Nujoma">Sam Nujoma</a> was sworn in as the first <a href="/wiki/President_of_Namibia" title="President of Namibia">President of Namibia</a> at a ceremony attended by <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Mandela" title="Nelson Mandela">Nelson Mandela</a> of South Africa (who had been released from prison the previous month) and representatives from 147 countries, including 20 heads of state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> Upon the end of <a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">Apartheid</a> in South Africa in 1994, the nation ceded <a href="/wiki/Walvis_Bay" title="Walvis Bay">Walvis Bay</a> to Namibia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="After_independence">After independence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: After independence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Since independence Namibia has completed the transition from white minority apartheid rule to parliamentary democracy. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multiparty_democracy" title="Multiparty democracy">Multiparty democracy</a> was introduced and has been maintained, with local, regional and <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Namibia" title="Elections in Namibia">national elections</a> held regularly. Several registered political parties are active and represented in the National Assembly, although the <a href="/wiki/SWAPO" title="SWAPO">SWAPO</a> has won every election since independence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> The transition from the 15-year rule of President <a href="/wiki/Sam_Nujoma" title="Sam Nujoma">Sam Nujoma</a> to his successor <a href="/wiki/Hifikepunye_Pohamba" title="Hifikepunye Pohamba">Hifikepunye Pohamba</a> in 2005 went smoothly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IRIN_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-IRIN-57">[57]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since independence, the Namibian government has promoted a policy of national reconciliation. It issued an amnesty for those who had fought on either side during the liberation war. The civil war in Angola spilled over and adversely affected Namibians living in the north of the country. In 1998, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Namibia_Defence_Force" title="Namibia Defence Force">Namibia Defence Force</a> (NDF) troops were sent to the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> as part of a <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Development_Community" title="Southern African Development Community">Southern African Development Community</a> (SADC) contingent.\n</p><p>In 1999, the national government quashed a secessionist attempt in the northeastern <a href="/wiki/Caprivi_Strip" title="Caprivi Strip">Caprivi Strip</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IRIN_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-IRIN-57">[57]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Caprivi_conflict" title="Caprivi conflict">Caprivi conflict</a> was initiated by the <a href="/wiki/Caprivi_Liberation_Army" title="Caprivi Liberation Army">Caprivi Liberation Army</a> (CLA), a <a href="/wiki/Rebellion" title="Rebellion">rebel</a> group led by <a href="/wiki/Mishake_Muyongo" title="Mishake Muyongo">Mishake Muyongo</a>. It wanted the Caprivi Strip to secede in order to form its own society.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Namibia" title="Geography of Namibia">Geography of Namibia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Namib_Desert_Namibia(2).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Namib_Desert_Namibia%282%29.jpg/220px-Namib_Desert_Namibia%282%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Namib_Desert_Namibia%282%29.jpg/330px-Namib_Desert_Namibia%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Namib_Desert_Namibia%282%29.jpg/440px-Namib_Desert_Namibia%282%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Namib_Desert_Namibia(2).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sand dunes in the <a href="/wiki/Namib" title="Namib">Namib</a>, Namibia</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Namibia_Natural_Earth_1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="914" data-file-width="1015" decoding="async" height="198" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Namibia_Natural_Earth_1.jpg/220px-Namibia_Natural_Earth_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Namibia_Natural_Earth_1.jpg/330px-Namibia_Natural_Earth_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Namibia_Natural_Earth_1.jpg/440px-Namibia_Natural_Earth_1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Namibia_Natural_Earth_1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Shaded relief map of Namibia</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Namibia_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1900" data-file-width="1900" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Namibia_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/220px-Namibia_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Namibia_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/330px-Namibia_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Namibia_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/440px-Namibia_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Namibia_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Namibia map of K&#246;ppen climate classification</div></div></div>\n<p>At 825,615&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (318,772&#160;sq&#160;mi),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> Namibia is the world\'s thirty-fourth largest country (after Venezuela). It lies mostly between latitudes <a href="/wiki/17th_parallel_south" title="17th parallel south">17&#176;</a> and <a href="/wiki/29th_parallel_south" title="29th parallel south">29&#176;S</a> (a small area is north of 17&#176;), and longitudes <a href="/wiki/11th_meridian_east" title="11th meridian east">11&#176;</a> and <a href="/wiki/26th_meridian_east" title="26th meridian east">26&#176;E</a>.\n</p><p>Being situated between the <a href="/wiki/Namib" title="Namib">Namib</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Kalahari_Desert" title="Kalahari Desert">Kalahari</a> deserts, Namibia has the least rainfall of any country in sub-Saharan Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Namibian landscape consists generally of five geographical areas, each with characteristic <a href="/wiki/Abiotic_component" title="Abiotic component">abiotic conditions</a> and vegetation, with some variation within and overlap between them: the Central Plateau, the Namib, the <a href="/wiki/Great_Escarpment,_Southern_Africa" title="Great Escarpment, Southern Africa">Great Escarpment</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bushveld" title="Bushveld">Bushveld</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Kalahari_Desert" title="Kalahari Desert">Kalahari Desert</a>.\n</p><p>The Central Plateau runs from north to south, bordered by the <a href="/wiki/Skeleton_Coast" title="Skeleton Coast">Skeleton Coast</a> to the northwest, the Namib Desert and its coastal plains to the southwest, the <a href="/wiki/Orange_River" title="Orange River">Orange River</a> to the south, and the Kalahari Desert to the east. The Central Plateau is home to the highest point in Namibia at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/K%C3%B6nigstein,_Namibia" title="K&#246;nigstein, Namibia">K&#246;nigstein</a> elevation 2,606 metres (8,550&#160;ft).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-elevation_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-elevation-60">[60]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Namib is a broad expanse of hyper-arid gravel plains and dunes that stretches along Namibia\'s entire coastline. It varies between 100 and many hundreds of kilometres in width. Areas within the Namib include the Skeleton Coast and the <a href="/wiki/Kaokoveld" title="Kaokoveld">Kaokoveld</a> in the north and the extensive Namib Sand Sea along the central coast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-at1315_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-at1315-20">[20]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Great Escarpment swiftly rises to over 2,000 metres (6,562&#160;ft). Average temperatures and temperature ranges increase further inland from the cold <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atlantic" title="Atlantic">Atlantic</a> waters, while the lingering coastal fogs slowly diminish. Although the area is rocky with poorly developed soils, it is significantly more productive than the Namib Desert. As summer winds are forced over the Escarpment, moisture is extracted as precipitation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Bushveld is found in north-eastern Namibia along the Angolan border and in the <a href="/wiki/Caprivi_Strip" title="Caprivi Strip">Caprivi Strip</a>. The area receives a significantly greater amount of precipitation than the rest of the country, averaging around 400&#160;mm (15.7&#160;in) per year. The area is generally flat and the soils sandy, limiting their ability to retain water and support agriculture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cowling,_S._2001_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cowling,_S._2001-62">[62]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Kalahari_Desert" title="Kalahari Desert">Kalahari Desert</a>, an arid region that extends into South Africa and Botswana, is one of Namibia\'s well-known geographical features. The Kalahari, while popularly known as a desert, has a variety of localised environments, including some verdant and technically non-desert areas. The <a href="/wiki/Succulent_Karoo" title="Succulent Karoo">Succulent Karoo</a> is home to over 5,000 species of plants, nearly half of them endemic; approximately 10 percent of the world\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Succulents" title="Succulents">succulents</a> are found in the Karoo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> The reason behind this high productivity and endemism may be the relatively stable nature of precipitation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Namibia\'s Coastal Desert is one of the oldest deserts in the world. Its sand dunes, created by the strong onshore winds, are the highest in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> Because of the location of the shoreline, at the point where the Atlantic\'s cold water reaches Africa\'s hot climate, often extremely dense fog forms along the coast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> Near the coast there are areas where the dunes are vegetated with <a href="/wiki/Hammock_(ecology)" title="Hammock (ecology)">hammocks</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> Namibia has rich coastal and marine resources that remain largely unexplored.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sparks_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sparks-68">[68]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SAC_Namibia-cactus.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="614" data-file-width="822" decoding="async" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/SAC_Namibia-cactus.jpg/220px-SAC_Namibia-cactus.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/SAC_Namibia-cactus.jpg/330px-SAC_Namibia-cactus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/SAC_Namibia-cactus.jpg/440px-SAC_Namibia-cactus.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SAC_Namibia-cactus.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Fish_River_Canyon" title="Fish River Canyon">Fish River Canyon</a></div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Namibia-1113.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Namibia-1113.jpg/220px-Namibia-1113.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Namibia-1113.jpg/330px-Namibia-1113.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Namibia-1113.jpg/440px-Namibia-1113.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Namibia-1113.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Namibia is primarily a large desert and semi-desert plateau.</div></div></div>\n<p>Namibia extends from 17&#176;S to 25&#176;S latitude: climatically the range of the sub-Tropical High Pressure Belt. Its overall climate description is arid, descending from the Sub-Humid [mean rain above 500&#160;mm (20&#160;in)] through Semi-Arid [between 300 and 500&#160;mm (12 and 20&#160;in)] (embracing most of the waterless Kalahari) and Arid [from 150 to 300&#160;mm (6 to 12&#160;in)] (these three regions are inland from the western <a href="/wiki/Great_Escarpment,_Southern_Africa" title="Great Escarpment, Southern Africa">escarpment</a>) to the Hyper-Arid coastal plain [less than 100&#160;mm (4&#160;in)]. Temperature maxima are limited by the overall elevation of the entire region: only in the far south, <a href="/wiki/Warmbad,_Namibia" title="Warmbad, Namibia">Warmbad</a> for instance, are mid-40&#160;&#176;C (100&#160;&#176;F) maxima recorded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Typically the sub-Tropical High Pressure Belt, with frequent clear skies, provides more than 300 days of sunshine per year. It is situated at the southern edge of the tropics; the <a href="/wiki/Tropic_of_Capricorn" title="Tropic of Capricorn">Tropic of Capricorn</a> cuts the country about in half. The winter (June&#160;&#8211; August) is generally dry. Both rainy seasons occur in summer: the small rainy season between September and November, the big one between February and April.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> Humidity is low, and average rainfall varies from almost zero in the <a href="/wiki/Skeleton_Coast" title="Skeleton Coast">coastal desert</a> to more than 600&#160;mm (24&#160;in) in the <a href="/wiki/Caprivi_Strip" title="Caprivi Strip">Caprivi Strip</a>. Rainfall is highly variable, and droughts are common.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EBClimate_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-EBClimate-71">[71]</a></sup> The last<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> rainy season with rainfall far below the annual average occurred in summer 2006/07.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Olszewski1_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-Olszewski1-72">[72]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Weather and climate in the coastal area are dominated by the cold, north-flowing <a href="/wiki/Benguela_Current" title="Benguela Current">Benguela Current</a> of the Atlantic Ocean, which accounts for very low <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">precipitation</a> (50&#160;mm (2&#160;in) per year or less), frequent dense fog, and overall lower temperatures than in the rest of the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EBClimate_71-1"><a href="#cite_note-EBClimate-71">[71]</a></sup> In Winter, occasionally a condition known as <i><i lang="de" title="German language text"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bergwind" title="Bergwind">Bergwind</a></i></i> (German for "mountain breeze") or <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">Oosweer</i></i> (<a href="/wiki/Afrikaans" title="Afrikaans">Afrikaans</a> for "east weather") occurs, a hot dry wind blowing from the inland to the coast. As the area behind the coast is a desert, these winds can develop into sand storms, leaving sand deposits in the Atlantic Ocean that are visible on satellite images.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Olszewski2_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-Olszewski2-73">[73]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Central Plateau and Kalahari areas have wide <a href="/wiki/Diurnal_temperature_variation" title="Diurnal temperature variation">diurnal</a> temperature ranges of up to 30&#160;&#176;C (54&#160;&#176;F).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EBClimate_71-2"><a href="#cite_note-EBClimate-71">[71]</a></sup>\n</p><p><i>Efundja</i>, the annual seasonal flooding of the northern parts of the country, often causes not only damage to infrastructure but loss of life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> The rains that cause these floods originate in Angola, flow into Namibia\'s <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Cuvelai_basin&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Cuvelai basin (page does not exist)">Cuvelai basin</a>, and fill the <i>oshanas</i> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oshiwambo" title="Oshiwambo">Oshiwambo</a>: flood plains) there. The worst floods so far<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> occurred in March 2011 and displaced 21,000 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_sources">Water sources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Water sources">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_Namibia" title="Water supply and sanitation in Namibia">Water supply and sanitation in Namibia</a></div>\n<p>Namibia is the driest country in <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">sub-Saharan Africa</a> and depends largely on groundwater. With an average rainfall of about 350&#160;mm (14&#160;in) per annum, the highest rainfall occurs in the <a href="/wiki/Caprivi_Strip" title="Caprivi Strip">Caprivi</a> in the northeast (about 600&#160;mm (24&#160;in) per annum) and decreases in a westerly and southwesterly direction to as little as 50&#160;mm (2&#160;in) and less per annum at the coast. The only perennial rivers are found on the national borders with <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">Zambia</a>, and the short border with <a href="/wiki/Botswana" title="Botswana">Botswana</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Caprivi_Strip" title="Caprivi Strip">Caprivi</a>. In the interior of the country, surface water is available only in the summer months when rivers are in flood after exceptional rainfalls. Otherwise, surface water is restricted to a few large storage dams retaining and damming up these seasonal floods and their runoff. Where people do not live near perennial rivers or make use of the storage dams, they are dependent on groundwater. Even isolated communities and those economic activities located far from good surface water sources, such as mining, agriculture, and tourism, can be supplied from groundwater over nearly 80% of the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup>\n</p><p>More than 100,000 <a href="/wiki/Borehole" title="Borehole">boreholes</a> have been drilled in Namibia over the past century. One third of these boreholes have been drilled dry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Communal_Wildlife_Conservancies">Communal Wildlife Conservancies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Communal Wildlife Conservancies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SAC_Namibia-bushveld.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="333" data-file-width="864" decoding="async" height="85" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/SAC_Namibia-bushveld.jpg/220px-SAC_Namibia-bushveld.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/SAC_Namibia-bushveld.jpg/330px-SAC_Namibia-bushveld.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/SAC_Namibia-bushveld.jpg/440px-SAC_Namibia-bushveld.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SAC_Namibia-bushveld.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Quivertree Forest, <a href="/wiki/Bushveld" title="Bushveld">Bushveld</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Communal_Wildlife_Conservancies_in_Namibia" title="Communal Wildlife Conservancies in Namibia">Communal Wildlife Conservancies in Namibia</a></div>\n<p>Namibia is one of few countries in the world to specifically address <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_conservation" title="Wildlife conservation">conservation</a> and protection of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Natural_resources" title="Natural resources">natural resources</a> in its constitution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stefanova_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-Stefanova-78">[78]</a></sup> Article 95 states, "The State shall actively promote and maintain the welfare of the people by adopting international policies aimed at the following: maintenance of <a href="/wiki/Ecology" title="Ecology">ecosystems</a>, essential ecological processes, and biological diversity of Namibia, and utilisation of living natural resources on a sustainable basis for the benefit of all Namibians, both present and future."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stefanova_78-1"><a href="#cite_note-Stefanova-78">[78]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1993, the newly formed government of Namibia received funding from the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Agency_for_International_Development" title="United States Agency for International Development">United States Agency for International Development</a> (USAID) through its Living in a Finite Environment (LIFE) Project.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> The Ministry of Environment and Tourism, with the financial support from organisations such as USAID, <a href="/wiki/Endangered_Wildlife_Trust" title="Endangered Wildlife Trust">Endangered Wildlife Trust</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Fund_for_Nature" title="World Wide Fund for Nature">WWF</a>, and Canadian Ambassador\'s Fund, together form a Community Based Natural Resource Management (CBNRM) support structure. The main goal of this project is promote sustainable natural resource management by giving local communities rights to wildlife management and tourism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNEP_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNEP-80">[80]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics_and_government">Politics and government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Politics and government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tintenpalast-Windhoek.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="533" data-file-width="840" decoding="async" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Tintenpalast-Windhoek.jpg/220px-Tintenpalast-Windhoek.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Tintenpalast-Windhoek.jpg/330px-Tintenpalast-Windhoek.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Tintenpalast-Windhoek.jpg/440px-Tintenpalast-Windhoek.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tintenpalast-Windhoek.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><center><a href="/wiki/Tintenpalast" title="Tintenpalast">Tintenpalast</a>, the centre of Namibia\'s government</center></div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Namibia" title="Politics of Namibia">Politics of Namibia</a></div>\n<p>Namibia is a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary</a> <a href="/wiki/Semi-presidential_system" title="Semi-presidential system">semi-presidential</a> <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democratic</a> <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Draft_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-Draft-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dual_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-Dual-11">[11]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Namibia" title="President of Namibia">President of Namibia</a> is elected to a five-year term and is both the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CN_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-CN-81">[81]</a></sup> However, while the President is both head of state and government, all members of the government are individually and collectively responsible to the legislature.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Namibia" title="Constitution of Namibia">Constitution of Namibia</a> guarantees the <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_powers" title="Separation of powers">separation of powers</a>:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-B&#246;sl_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-B&#246;sl-83">[83]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>Executive: Executive power is exercised by the President and the <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Namibia" title="Cabinet of Namibia">Government</a>.</li>\n<li>Legislature: Namibia has a <a href="/wiki/Bicameralism" title="Bicameralism">bicameral</a> <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Namibia" title="Parliament of Namibia">Parliament</a> with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Namibia" title="National Assembly of Namibia">National Assembly</a> as <a href="/wiki/Lower_house" title="Lower house">lower house</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Council_of_Namibia" title="National Council of Namibia">National Council</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Upper_house" title="Upper house">upper house</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parliament153_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-parliament153-12">[12]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">Judiciary</a>: Namibia has a system of courts that interpret and apply the law in the name of the state.</li></ul>\n<p>While the constitution envisaged a <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">multi-party system</a> for Namibia\'s government, the <a href="/wiki/SWAPO" title="SWAPO">SWAPO</a> party has been <a href="/wiki/Dominant-party_system" title="Dominant-party system">dominant</a> since independence in 1990.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Namibia" title="Foreign relations of Namibia">Foreign relations of Namibia</a></div>\n<p>Namibia follows a largely independent <a href="/wiki/Foreign_policy" title="Foreign policy">foreign policy</a>, with persisting affiliations with states that aided the independence struggle, including <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>. With a small army and a fragile economy, the Namibian Government\'s principal foreign policy concern is developing strengthened ties within the Southern African region. A dynamic member of the <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Development_Community" title="Southern African Development Community">Southern African Development Community</a>, Namibia is a vocal advocate for greater regional integration. Namibia became the 160th member of the UN on 23 April 1990. On its independence it became the fiftieth member of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Namibian_Defence_Force" title="Namibian Defence Force">Namibian Defence Force</a></div>\n<table class="box-Update plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="Ambox current red.svg" data-file-height="290" data-file-width="360" decoding="async" height="34" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" width="42"/></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section needs to be <b>updated</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">March 2015</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Namibia does not have any enemies in <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Development_Community" title="Southern African Development Community">the region</a> although it has been involved in various disputes regarding borders and construction plans.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> It consistently spends more as a percentage of GDP on its military than all of its neighbours, except Angola. Military expenditure rose from 2.7% of GDP in 2000 to 3.7% in 2009, and the arrival of 12 <a href="/wiki/Chengdu_J-7" title="Chengdu J-7">Chengdu J-7 Airguard</a> jets in 2006 and 2008 made Namibia for a short time one of the top arms importers in Sub-Saharan Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-flying_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-flying-86">[86]</a></sup>  By 2015, military expenditure was estimated at between 4% and 5% of GDP.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Insight2015_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-Insight2015-87">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The constitution of Namibia defined the role of the military as "<i>defending the territory and national interests.</i>" Namibia formed the <a href="/wiki/Namibian_Defence_Force" title="Namibian Defence Force">Namibian Defence Force</a> (NDF), comprising former enemies in a 23-year bush war: the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Liberation_Army_of_Namibia" title="People\'s Liberation Army of Namibia">People\'s Liberation Army of Namibia</a> (PLAN) and <a href="/wiki/South_West_Africa" title="South West Africa">South West African</a> <i>Territorial Force</i> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SWATF" title="SWATF">SWATF</a>). The British formulated the plan for integrating these forces and began training the NDF, which consists of a small headquarters and five battalions.\n</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_Transitional_Assistance_Group" title="United Nations Transitional Assistance Group">United Nations Transitional Assistance Group</a> (UNTAG)\'s Kenyan infantry battalion remained in Namibia for three months after independence to help train the NDF and to stabilise the north. According to the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Namibian_Defence_Ministry&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Namibian Defence Ministry (page does not exist)">Namibian Defence Ministry</a>, enlistments of both men and women will number no more than 7,500. The current minister of the Namibian Military is Hon Penda YaNdakolo\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lettered_Namibia_Regions1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="859" data-file-width="878" decoding="async" height="215" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Lettered_Namibia_Regions1.jpg/220px-Lettered_Namibia_Regions1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Lettered_Namibia_Regions1.jpg/330px-Lettered_Namibia_Regions1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Lettered_Namibia_Regions1.jpg/440px-Lettered_Namibia_Regions1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lettered_Namibia_Regions1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The fourteen <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Namibia" title="Regions of Namibia">regions of Namibia</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Namibia" title="Administrative divisions of Namibia">Administrative divisions of Namibia</a></div>\n<p>Namibia is divided into 14 regions and subdivided into 121 constituencies. The administrative division of Namibia is tabled by <i>Delimitation Commissions</i> and accepted or declined by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Namibia" title="National Assembly of Namibia">National Assembly</a>. Since state foundation four Delimitation Commissions have delivered their work, the last one in 2013 under the chairmanship of Judge <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Alfred_Siboleka&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Alfred Siboleka (page does not exist)">Alfred Siboleka</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Regional councillors are directly elected through secret ballots (regional elections) by the inhabitants of their constituencies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Local authorities in Namibia can be in the form of municipalities (either Part 1 or Part 2 municipalities), town councils or villages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-alan_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-alan-92">[92]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:left;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Namibia" title="Economy of Namibia">Economy of Namibia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Downtown_Windhoek,_Independence_Avenue.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="667" data-file-width="1000" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Downtown_Windhoek%2C_Independence_Avenue.jpg/220px-Downtown_Windhoek%2C_Independence_Avenue.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Downtown_Windhoek%2C_Independence_Avenue.jpg/330px-Downtown_Windhoek%2C_Independence_Avenue.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Downtown_Windhoek%2C_Independence_Avenue.jpg/440px-Downtown_Windhoek%2C_Independence_Avenue.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Downtown_Windhoek,_Independence_Avenue.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Downtown <a href="/wiki/Windhoek" title="Windhoek">Windhoek</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tsumeb-Main_Road.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Tsumeb-Main_Road.JPG/220px-Tsumeb-Main_Road.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Tsumeb-Main_Road.JPG/330px-Tsumeb-Main_Road.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Tsumeb-Main_Road.JPG/440px-Tsumeb-Main_Road.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tsumeb-Main_Road.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Tsumeb" title="Tsumeb">Tsumeb</a>\'s main road</div></div></div>\n<p>Namibia\'s economy is tied closely to <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_South_Africa" title="Economy of South Africa">South Africa\'s</a> due to their shared history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Intelligence1_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-Intelligence1-93">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Department1_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-Department1-94">[94]</a></sup> The largest economic sectors are mining (10.4% of the gross domestic product in 2009), agriculture (5.0%), manufacturing (13.5%), and tourism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usds_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-usds-95">[95]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Namibia has a highly developed banking sector with modern infrastructure, such as online banking and cellphone banking. The Bank of Namibia (BoN) is the central bank of Namibia responsible for performing all other functions ordinarily performed by a central bank. There are 5 BoN authorised commercial banks in Namibia: Bank Windhoek, First National Bank, Nedbank, Standard Bank and Small and Medium Enterprises Bank.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to the Namibia Labour Force Survey Report 2012, conducted by the <a class="extiw" href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Namibia_Statistics_Agency" title="de:Namibia Statistics Agency">Namibia Statistics Agency</a>, the country\'s unemployment rate is 27.4%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> "Strict unemployment" (people actively seeking a full-time job) stood at 20.2% in 2000, 21.9% in 2004 and spiraled to 29.4% in 2008. Under a broader definition (including people that have given up searching for employment) unemployment rose to 36.7% in 2004. This estimate considers people in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Informal_sector" title="Informal sector">informal economy</a> as employed. Labour and Social Welfare Minister <a href="/wiki/Immanuel_Ngatjizeko" title="Immanuel Ngatjizeko">Immanuel Ngatjizeko</a> praised the 2008 study as "by far superior in scope and quality to any that has been available previously",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> but its methodology has also received criticism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2004 a labour act was passed to protect people from job discrimination stemming from pregnancy and HIV/AIDS status. In early 2010 the Government <a href="/wiki/Tender_board" title="Tender board">tender board</a> announced that "henceforth 100 per cent of all unskilled and semi-skilled labour must be sourced, without exception, from within Namibia".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2013, global business and financial news provider, <a href="/wiki/Bloomberg_L.P." title="Bloomberg L.P.">Bloomberg</a>, named Namibia the top emerging market economy in Africa and the 13th best in the world. Only four African countries made the Top 20 Emerging Markets list in the March 2013 issue of Bloomberg Markets magazine, and Namibia was rated ahead of <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a> (19th), South Africa (15th) and <a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">Zambia</a> (14th). Worldwide, Namibia also fared better than Hungary, Brazil and Mexico. Bloomberg Markets magazine ranked the top 20 based on more than a dozen criteria. The data came from Bloomberg\'s own financial-market statistics, IMF forecasts and the World Bank. The countries were also rated on areas of particular interest to foreign investors: the ease of doing business, the perceived level of corruption and economic freedom. In order to attract foreign investment, the government has made improvement in reducing red tape resulted from excessive government regulations making the country one of the least bureaucratic places to do business in the region. However, facilitation payments are occasionally demanded by customs due to cumbersome and costly customs procedures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> Namibia is also classified as an Upper Middle Income country by the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, and ranks 87th out of 185 economies in terms of ease of doing business.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Cost_of_living_in_Namibia" title="Cost of living in Namibia">cost of living in Namibia</a> is relatively high because most of the goods including cereals need to be imported. Its capital city, Windhoek is currently ranked as the 150th most expensive place in the world for expatriates to live.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Taxation_in_Namibia" title="Taxation in Namibia">Taxation in Namibia</a> includes personal income tax, which is applicable to total taxable income of an individual and all individuals are taxed at progressive marginal rates over a series of income brackets. The value added tax (VAT) is applicable to most of the commodities and services.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sandstorm_while_driving_from_Swakopmund_to_Walfish_Bay,_2005.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Sandstorm_while_driving_from_Swakopmund_to_Walfish_Bay%2C_2005.jpg/220px-Sandstorm_while_driving_from_Swakopmund_to_Walfish_Bay%2C_2005.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Sandstorm_while_driving_from_Swakopmund_to_Walfish_Bay%2C_2005.jpg/330px-Sandstorm_while_driving_from_Swakopmund_to_Walfish_Bay%2C_2005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Sandstorm_while_driving_from_Swakopmund_to_Walfish_Bay%2C_2005.jpg/440px-Sandstorm_while_driving_from_Swakopmund_to_Walfish_Bay%2C_2005.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sandstorm_while_driving_from_Swakopmund_to_Walfish_Bay,_2005.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/B2_road_(Namibia)" title="B2 road (Namibia)">B2</a> between <a href="/wiki/Swakopmund" title="Swakopmund">Swakopmund</a> and <a href="/wiki/Walvis_Bay" title="Walvis Bay">Walvis Bay</a>, Namibia</div></div></div>\n<p>Despite the remote nature of much of the country, Namibia has seaports, airports, highways, and <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Namibia" title="Rail transport in Namibia">railways</a> (narrow-gauge). The country seeks to become a regional transportation hub; it has an important seaport and several landlocked neighbours.
