The Central Plateau already serves as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transportation_corridor" title="Transportation corridor">transportation corridor</a> from the more densely populated north to South Africa, the source of four-fifths of Namibia\'s imports.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_Almanac_2004_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-World_Almanac_2004-105">[105]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Income_disparity">Income disparity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Income disparity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>According to recent statistics on the country\'s income share held by the highest 10%, Namibia is a country with a substantive income disparity. The data indicates that the current income share held by the highest 10% is approximately 51.8%. This disparity that exists in the country illustrates the large gap between the rich and the poor. An additional figure describes the poverty gap: people living on US$2 or less in the country are approximately 17.72% of the population.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Agriculture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Namibia" title="Agriculture in Namibia">Agriculture in Namibia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Schildburgsdorf.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="167" data-file-width="326" decoding="async" height="113" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Schildburgsdorf.jpg/220px-Schildburgsdorf.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/13/Schildburgsdorf.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Schildburgsdorf.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Welcoming sign of the <i>Burgsdorf</i> farm in <a href="/wiki/Hardap_Region" title="Hardap Region">Hardap</a></div></div></div>\n<p>About half of the population depends on agriculture (largely <a href="/wiki/Subsistence_agriculture" title="Subsistence agriculture">subsistence agriculture</a>) for its livelihood, but Namibia must still import some of its food. Although per capita GDP is five times the per capita GDP of Africa\'s poorest countries, the majority of Namibia\'s people live in rural areas and exist on a subsistence way of life. Namibia has one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_income_equality" title="List of countries by income equality">highest rates of income inequality</a> in the world, due in part to the fact that there is an urban economy and a more rural cashless economy. The inequality figures thus take into account people who do not actually rely on the formal economy for their survival. Although arable land accounts for only 1% of Namibia, nearly half of the population is employed in agriculture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_Almanac_2004_105-1"><a href="#cite_note-World_Almanac_2004-105">[105]</a></sup>\n</p><p>About 4,000, mostly white, commercial farmers own almost half of Namibia\'s arable land.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> The governments of Germany and Britain will finance Namibia\'s <a href="/wiki/Land_reform" title="Land reform">land reform</a> process, as Namibia plans to start expropriating land from white farmers to resettle landless black Namibians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Agreement has been reached on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Privatisation" title="Privatisation">privatisation</a> of several more enterprises in coming years, with hopes that this will stimulate much needed foreign investment. However, reinvestment of environmentally derived capital has hobbled Namibian per capita income.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lange_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lange-108">[108]</a></sup> One of the fastest growing areas of economic development in Namibia is the growth of <a href="/wiki/Communal_Wildlife_Conservancies_in_Namibia" title="Communal Wildlife Conservancies in Namibia">wildlife conservancies</a>. These conservancies are particularly important to the rural, generally unemployed, population.\n</p><p>An <a href="/wiki/Aquifer" title="Aquifer">aquifer</a> called "Ohangwena II", located on both sides of the Angola-Namibia border, was discovered in 2012.  This aquifer has been estimated to be capable of supplying the 800,000 people in the North for 400 years, at the current (2018) rate of consumption.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aqui_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-aqui-109">[109]</a></sup> Experts estimate that Namibia has 7,720&#160;km<sup>3</sup> (1,850&#160;cu&#160;mi) of underground water.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-afr_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-afr-110">[110]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aqmap_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-aqmap-111">[111]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mining_and_electricity">Mining and electricity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Mining and electricity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mining_in_Namibia" title="Mining in Namibia">Mining in Namibia</a></div>\n<p>Providing 25% of Namibia\'s revenue, mining is the single most important contributor to the economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> Namibia is the fourth largest exporter of non-fuel minerals in Africa and the world\'s fourth largest producer of <a href="/wiki/Uranium" title="Uranium">uranium</a>. There has been significant investment in <a href="/wiki/Uranium_mining" title="Uranium mining">uranium mining</a> and Namibia is set to become the largest exporter of uranium by 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> Rich <a href="/wiki/Alluvium" title="Alluvium">alluvial</a> diamond deposits make Namibia a primary source for gem-quality diamonds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> While Namibia is known predominantly for its gem diamond and uranium deposits, a number of other minerals are extracted industrially such as <a href="/wiki/Lead" title="Lead">lead</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tungsten" title="Tungsten">tungsten</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tin" title="Tin">tin</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fluorspar" title="Fluorspar">fluorspar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manganese" title="Manganese">manganese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marble" title="Marble">marble</a>, <a href="/wiki/Copper" title="Copper">copper</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zinc" title="Zinc">zinc</a>. There are offshore gas deposits in the Atlantic Ocean that are planned to be extracted in the future.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usds_95-1"><a href="#cite_note-usds-95">[95]</a></sup> According to "The Diamond Investigation", a book about the global diamond market, from 1978, <a href="/wiki/De_Beers" title="De Beers">De Beers</a>, the largest diamond company, bought most of the Namibian diamonds, and would continue to do so, because "whatever government eventually comes to power they will need this revenue to survive".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Domestic supply voltage is 220 V AC. Electricity is generated mainly by thermal and hydroelectric power plants. Non-conventional methods of electricity generation also play some role. Encouraged by the rich uranium deposits the Namibian government plans to erect its first nuclear power station by 2018, also uranium enrichment is envisaged to happen locally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Saveorsink_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-Saveorsink-116">[116]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Diamonds">Diamonds</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Diamonds">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Although much of the world\'s diamond supply comes from what have been called African <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blood_diamonds" title="Blood diamonds">blood diamonds</a>, Namibia has managed to develop a diamond mining industry largely free of the kinds of conflict, extortion, and murder that have surrounded that of many other African nations with diamond mines.  This has been attributed to political dynamics, economic institutions, grievances, political geography, and the effects of neighborhoods, and is the result of a joint agreement between the government and <a href="/wiki/De_Beers" title="De Beers">De Beers</a> which has led to a taxable base, strengthening state institutions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Namibia" title="Tourism in Namibia">Tourism in Namibia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Equus_burchelli_4.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2056" data-file-width="2742" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Equus_burchelli_4.jpg/220px-Equus_burchelli_4.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Equus_burchelli_4.jpg/330px-Equus_burchelli_4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Equus_burchelli_4.jpg/440px-Equus_burchelli_4.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Equus_burchelli_4.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An example of Namibian wildlife, the <a href="/wiki/Plains_zebra" title="Plains zebra">plains zebra</a>, is one focus of tourism.</div></div></div>\n<p>Tourism is a major contributor (14.5%) to Namibia\'s GDP, creating tens of thousands of jobs (18.2% of all employment) directly or indirectly and servicing over a million tourists per year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> The country is a prime destination in Africa and is known for <a href="/wiki/Ecotourism" title="Ecotourism">ecotourism</a> which features <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Namibia" title="Wildlife of Namibia">Namibia\'s extensive wildlife</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-goodshape_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-goodshape-119">[119]</a></sup>\n</p><p>There are many lodges and reserves to accommodate eco-tourists. Sport and <a href="/wiki/Trophy_hunting" title="Trophy hunting">trophy hunting</a> is also a large, and growing component of the Namibian economy, accounting for 14% of total tourism in the year 2000, or $19.6&#160;million US dollars, with Namibia boasting numerous species sought after by international sport hunters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Humavindu_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-Humavindu-120">[120]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In addition, extreme sports such as <a href="/wiki/Sandboarding" title="Sandboarding">sandboarding</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Skydiving" title="Skydiving">skydiving</a> and 4x4ing have become popular, and many cities have companies that provide tours.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The most visited places include the capital city of <a href="/wiki/Windhoek" title="Windhoek">Windhoek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caprivi_Strip" title="Caprivi Strip">Caprivi Strip</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fish_River_Canyon" title="Fish River Canyon">Fish River Canyon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sossusvlei" title="Sossusvlei">Sossusvlei</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Skeleton_Coast" title="Skeleton Coast">Skeleton Coast</a> Park, <a href="/wiki/Sesriem" title="Sesriem">Sesriem</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Etosha_Pan" title="Etosha Pan">Etosha Pan</a> and the coastal towns of <a href="/wiki/Swakopmund" title="Swakopmund">Swakopmund</a>, <a href="/wiki/Walvis_Bay" title="Walvis Bay">Walvis Bay</a> and <a href="/wiki/L%C3%BCderitz" title="L&#252;deritz">L&#252;deritz</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The capital city of Windhoek plays a very important role in Namibia\'s tourism due to its central location and close proximity to <a href="/wiki/Hosea_Kutako_International_Airport" title="Hosea Kutako International Airport">Hosea Kutako International Airport</a>. According to The Namibia Tourism Exit Survey, which was produced by the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Challenge_Corporation" title="Millennium Challenge Corporation">Millennium Challenge Corporation</a> for the Namibian Directorate of Tourism, 56% of all tourists visiting Namibia during the time period, 2012&#160;&#8211; 2013, visited Windhoek.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> Many of Namibia\'s tourism related parastatals and governing bodies such as Namibia Wildlife Resorts, <a href="/wiki/Air_Namibia" title="Air Namibia">Air Namibia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Namibia_Tourism_Board" title="Namibia Tourism Board">Namibia Tourism Board</a> as well as Namibia\'s tourism related <a href="/wiki/Trade_association" title="Trade association">trade associations</a> such as the <a href="/wiki/Hospitality_Association_of_Namibia" title="Hospitality Association of Namibia">Hospitality Association of Namibia</a> are also all headquartered in Windhoek.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> There are also a number of notable hotels in Windhoek such as <a href="/wiki/Windhoek_Country_Club_Resort" title="Windhoek Country Club Resort">Windhoek Country Club Resort</a> and some international hotel chains also operate in Windhoek, such as Avani Hotels and Resorts and <a href="/wiki/Hilton_Hotels_%26_Resorts" title="Hilton Hotels &amp; Resorts">Hilton Hotels and Resorts</a>.\n</p><p>Namibia\'s primary tourism related governing body, the <a href="/wiki/Namibia_Tourism_Board" title="Namibia Tourism Board">Namibia Tourism Board</a> (NTB), was established by an Act of Parliament: the Namibia Tourism Board Act, 2000 (Act 21 of 2000). Its primary objectives are to regulate the tourism industry and to market Namibia as a tourist destination.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> There are also a number of <a href="/wiki/Trade_association" title="Trade association">trade associations</a> that represent the tourism sector in Namibia, such as the Federation of Namibia Tourism Associations (the umbrella body for all tourism associations in Namibia), the <a href="/wiki/Hospitality_Association_of_Namibia" title="Hospitality Association of Namibia">Hospitality Association of Namibia</a>, the Association of Namibian Travel Agents, Car Rental Association of Namibia and the Tour and Safari Association of Namibia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_supply_and_sanitation">Water supply and sanitation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Water supply and sanitation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_Namibia" title="Water supply and sanitation in Namibia">Water supply and sanitation in Namibia</a></div>\n<p>Namibia is the only country in Sub-Saharan Africa to provide water through municipal departments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-126">[126]</a></sup> The only bulk water supplier in Namibia is <a href="/wiki/NamWater" title="NamWater">NamWater</a>, which sells it to the respective municipalities which in turn deliver it through their reticulation networks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_126-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-126">[126]</a></sup> In rural areas, the Directorate of Rural Water Supply in the Ministry of Agriculture, Water and Forestry is in charge of drinking water supply.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_126-2"><a href="#cite_note-:0-126">[126]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">UN</a> evaluated in 2011 that Namibia has improved its water access network significantly since independence\nin 1990. A large part of the population can not, however, make use of\nthese resources due to the prohibitively high consumption cost and the\nlong distance between residences and water points in rural areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_126-3"><a href="#cite_note-:0-126">[126]</a></sup> As a result, many Namibians prefer the traditional wells over the available water points far away.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-127">[127]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Compared to the efforts made to improve access to safe water, Namibia is lagging behind in the provision of adequate sanitation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> This includes 298 schools that have no toilet facilities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-:2-129">[129]</a></sup> Over 50% of child deaths are related to lack of water, sanitation, or hygiene; 23% are due to diarrhea alone. The UN has identified a "sanitation crisis" in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_127-1"><a href="#cite_note-:1-127">[127]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Apart from residences for upper and middle class households,\nsanitation is insufficient in most residential areas. Private flush\ntoilets are too expensive for virtually all residents in <a href="/wiki/Township" title="Township">townships</a> due to their water consumption and installation cost. As a result, access to <a href="/wiki/Improved_sanitation" title="Improved sanitation">improved sanitation</a> has not increased much since independence:\nIn Namibia\'s rural areas 13% of the population had more than basic\nsanitation, up from 8% in 1990. Many of Namibia\'s inhabitants have to\nresort to "flying toilets", plastic bags to defecate which after use are\nflung into the bush.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> The use of open areas close to residential land to urinate and defecate is very common<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> and has been identified as a major <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Namibia" title="Health in Namibia">health hazard</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_129-1"><a href="#cite_note-:2-129">[129]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Namibia" title="Demographics of Namibia">Demographics of Namibia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Namibia_Population_Density_(2011).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="744" data-file-width="836" decoding="async" height="196" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Namibia_Population_Density_%282011%29.jpg/220px-Namibia_Population_Density_%282011%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Namibia_Population_Density_%282011%29.jpg/330px-Namibia_Population_Density_%282011%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Namibia_Population_Density_%282011%29.jpg/440px-Namibia_Population_Density_%282011%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Namibia_Population_Density_(2011).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Population density in Namibia by regions (census 2011)</div></div></div>\n<table class="wikitable" style="float: right; margin-left: 10px">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="4" style="text-align:center; background:#cfb;">Population<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-132">[132]</a></sup>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="background:#cfb;">Year\n</th>\n<th style="background:#cfb;">Million\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">1950</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">0.5\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">2000</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">1.9\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">2016</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">2.5\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Namibia_2016.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="425" data-file-width="610" decoding="async" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Namibia_2016.png/220px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Namibia_2016.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Namibia_2016.png/330px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Namibia_2016.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Namibia_2016.png/440px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Namibia_2016.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Namibia_2016.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Population pyramid 2016</div></div></div>\n<p>Namibia has the second-<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_population_density" title="List of countries by population density">lowest population density</a> of any sovereign country, after <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unpop_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-unpop-133">[133]</a></sup> The majority of the Namibian population is of <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantu</a>-speaking origin &#160;&#8211; mostly of the <a href="/wiki/Ovambo_people" title="Ovambo people">Ovambo</a> ethnicity, which forms about half of the population&#160;&#8211; residing mainly in the north of the country, although many are now resident in towns throughout Namibia. Other ethnic groups are the <a href="/wiki/Herero_people" title="Herero people">Herero</a> and <a href="/wiki/Himba_people" title="Himba people">Himba people</a>, who speak a similar language, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Damara_(people)" title="Damara (people)">Damara</a>, who speak the same "click" language as the <a href="/wiki/Nama_people" title="Nama people">Nama</a>.\n</p><p>In addition to the Bantu majority, there are large groups of <a href="/wiki/Khoisan" title="Khoisan">Khoisan</a> (such as Nama and <a href="/wiki/San_people" title="San people">San</a>), who are descendants of the original inhabitants of Southern Africa. The country also contains some <a href="/wiki/Angolans_in_Namibia" title="Angolans in Namibia">descendants of refugees from Angola</a>. There are also two smaller groups of people with mixed racial origins, called "<a href="/wiki/Coloured_people_in_Namibia" title="Coloured people in Namibia">Coloureds</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Baster" title="Baster">Basters</a>", who together make up 8.0% (with the Coloureds outnumbering the Basters two to one). There is a substantial <a href="/wiki/Chinese_people_in_Namibia" title="Chinese people in Namibia">Chinese minority in Namibia</a>; it stood at 40,000 in 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Himba_Woman_and_Family.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3456" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Himba_Woman_and_Family.JPG/220px-Himba_Woman_and_Family.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Himba_Woman_and_Family.JPG/330px-Himba_Woman_and_Family.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Himba_Woman_and_Family.JPG/440px-Himba_Woman_and_Family.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Himba_Woman_and_Family.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Himba_people" title="Himba people">Himba people</a> in northern Namibia</div></div></div>\n<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_African" title="White African">Whites</a> (mainly of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afrikaner_people" title="Afrikaner people">Afrikaner</a>, German, British and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a> origin) make up between 4.0 and 7.0% of the population.  Although their percentage of population decreased after <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Independence_of_Namibia" title="Independence of Namibia">independence</a> due to emigration and lower birth rates, they still form the second-largest population of <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Europe" title="Ethnic groups in Europe">European ancestry</a>, both in terms of percentage and actual numbers, in <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan Africa</a> (after South Africa).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-135">[135]</a></sup> The majority of <a href="/wiki/White_Namibians" title="White Namibians">Namibian whites</a> and nearly all those who are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Basters" title="Basters">mixed race</a> speak <a href="/wiki/Afrikaans" title="Afrikaans">Afrikaans</a> and share similar origins, culture, and religion as the white and coloured populations of South Africa. A large minority of whites (around 30,000) trace their family origins back to the <a href="/wiki/German_Namibians" title="German Namibians">German</a> settlers who colonized Namibia prior to the British confiscation of German lands after World War One, and they maintain German cultural and educational institutions. Nearly all Portuguese settlers came to the country from the former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguese_West_Africa" title="Portuguese West Africa">Portuguese colony</a> of Angola.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> The 1960 census reported 526,004 persons in what was then South-West Africa, including 73,464 whites (14%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Children_in_Namibia(1_cropped).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1003" data-file-width="1353" decoding="async" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Children_in_Namibia%281_cropped%29.jpg/220px-Children_in_Namibia%281_cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Children_in_Namibia%281_cropped%29.jpg/330px-Children_in_Namibia%281_cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Children_in_Namibia%281_cropped%29.jpg/440px-Children_in_Namibia%281_cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Children_in_Namibia(1_cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Children in Namibia</div></div></div>\n<p>Namibia conducts a census every ten years. After independence the first Population and Housing Census was carried out in 1991; further rounds followed in 2001 and 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2001Census_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-2001Census-138">[138]</a></sup> The data collection method is to count every person resident in Namibia on the census reference night, wherever they happen to be. This is called the <i>de facto</i> method.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> For enumeration purposes the country is demarcated into 4,042 <i>enumeration areas</i>. These areas do not overlap with constituency boundaries to get reliable data for election purposes as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The 2011 Population and Housing Census counted 2,113,077 inhabitants of Namibia. Between 2001 and 2011 the annual population growth was 1.4%, down from 2.6% in the previous ten&#8211;year period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-snapshot_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-snapshot-141">[141]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Namibia" title="Religion in Namibia">Religion in Namibia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Swakopmund_ev-luth_Kirche_1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3684" data-file-width="5526" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Swakopmund_ev-luth_Kirche_1.jpg/220px-Swakopmund_ev-luth_Kirche_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Swakopmund_ev-luth_Kirche_1.jpg/330px-Swakopmund_ev-luth_Kirche_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Swakopmund_ev-luth_Kirche_1.jpg/440px-Swakopmund_ev-luth_Kirche_1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Swakopmund_ev-luth_Kirche_1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lutheran church in <a href="/wiki/Swakopmund" title="Swakopmund">Swakopmund</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The Christian community makes up 80%&#8211;90% of the population of Namibia, with at least 75% being <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant" title="Protestant">Protestant</a>, and at least 50% <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutheran</a>. Lutherans are the largest religious group&#160;&#8211; a legacy of the German and <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finnish</a> missionary work during the country\'s colonial times. 10%&#8211;20% of the population hold <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">indigenous</a> beliefs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_135-1"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-135">[135]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Missionary activities during the second half of the 19th century resulted in many Namibians converting to Christianity. Today most Christians are Lutheran, but there also are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Methodism" title="Methodism">Methodist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anglicanism" title="Anglicanism">Anglican</a>, <a href="/wiki/African_Methodist_Episcopal_Church" title="African Methodist Episcopal Church">African Methodist Episcopal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Reformed_Church" title="Dutch Reformed Church">Dutch Reformed</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mormonism" title="Mormonism">Mormons</a> (<a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints</a>).\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Namibia" title="Islam in Namibia">Islam in Namibia</a> is subscribed to by about 9,000 Muslims,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> many of whom are Nama.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> Namibia is home to a small <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Jewish</a> community of about 100 members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jewishvirtuallibrary1_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-jewishvirtuallibrary1-144">[144]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Namibia" title="Languages of Namibia">Languages of Namibia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NamibiaMehrsprachigkeit.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="595" data-file-width="914" decoding="async" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/NamibiaMehrsprachigkeit.jpg/220px-NamibiaMehrsprachigkeit.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/NamibiaMehrsprachigkeit.jpg/330px-NamibiaMehrsprachigkeit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/NamibiaMehrsprachigkeit.jpg/440px-NamibiaMehrsprachigkeit.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NamibiaMehrsprachigkeit.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Although its official language is English, Namibia is a multilingual country as is illustrated by these examples in English, German, <a href="/wiki/Afrikaans" title="Afrikaans">Afrikaans</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oshiwambo_language" title="Oshiwambo language">Oshiwambo</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Up to 1990, English, <a href="/wiki/German_language_in_Namibia" title="German language in Namibia">German</a> and <a href="/wiki/Afrikaans" title="Afrikaans">Afrikaans</a> were official languages. Long before Namibia\'s independence from South Africa, SWAPO was of the opinion that the country should become officially monolingual, choosing this approach in contrast to that of its neighbour South Africa (which granted <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_South_Africa" title="Languages of South Africa">all 11 of its major languages</a> official status), which was seen by them as "a deliberate policy of ethnolinguistic fragmentation."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> Consequently, SWAPO instituted English as the sole official language of Namibia though only about 3% of the population speaks it as a home language. Its implementation is focused on the civil service, education and the broadcasting system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kriger_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-kriger-146">[146]</a></sup> Some other languages have received semi-official recognition by being allowed as medium of instruction in primary schools. It is expected of private schools to follow the same policy as state schools, and "English language" is a compulsory subject.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kriger_146-1"><a href="#cite_note-kriger-146">[146]</a></sup> Some critics however argue that, as in other postcolonial African societies, the push for monolingual instruction and policy has resulted in a high rate of school drop-outs and of individuals whose academic competence in any language is low.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to the 2011 census, the most common languages are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oshiwambo" title="Oshiwambo">Oshiwambo</a> (the most spoken language for 49% of households),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nama_language" title="Nama language">Nama</a>/<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Damara_language" title="Damara language">Damara</a> (11.3%), Afrikaans (10.4%), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kavango_languages" title="Kavango languages">Kavango</a> (9%), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Otjiherero" title="Otjiherero">Otjiherero</a> (9%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-snapshot_141-1"><a href="#cite_note-snapshot-141">[141]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-census2011_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-census2011-149">[149]</a></sup> However, the most widely understood national language is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afrikaans_language" title="Afrikaans language">Afrikaans</a>, which is the lingua franca of the country. Both Afrikaans and English are used primarily as a second language reserved for public communication.\n</p><p>Most of the white population speaks either German or Afrikaans. Even today, 104 years after the end of the German colonial era, the German language plays a role as a commercial language. Afrikaans is spoken by 60% of the white community, German is spoken by 32%, English is spoken by 7% and Portuguese by 4&#8211;5%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_135-2"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-135">[135]</a></sup> Geographical proximity to Portuguese-speaking Angola explains the relatively high number of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguese_speaker" title="Portuguese speaker">Portuguese speakers</a>; in 2011 these were estimated to be 100,000, or 4&#8211;5% of the total population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Largest_cities">Largest cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Largest cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_and_towns_in_Namibia" title="List of cities and towns in Namibia">List of cities and towns in Namibia</a></div>\n<table id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Namibia" title="Sport in Namibia">Sport in Namibia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union_in_Namibia" title="Rugby union in Namibia">Rugby union in Namibia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Namibia_Rugby_Team.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="900" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Namibia_Rugby_Team.jpg/170px-Namibia_Rugby_Team.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Namibia_Rugby_Team.jpg/255px-Namibia_Rugby_Team.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Namibia_Rugby_Team.jpg/340px-Namibia_Rugby_Team.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Namibia_Rugby_Team.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Namibia_national_rugby_union_team" title="Namibia national rugby union team">Namibia rugby team</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The most popular sport in Namibia is <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">association football</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Namibia_national_football_team" title="Namibia national football team">Namibia national football team</a> qualified for the <a href="/wiki/2008_Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="2008 Africa Cup of Nations">2008 Africa Cup of Nations</a> but has yet to qualify for any <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">World Cups</a>.\n</p><p>The most successful national team is the <a href="/wiki/Namibia_national_rugby_union_team" title="Namibia national rugby union team">Namibian rugby team</a>, having competed in five separate World Cups. Namibia were participants in the <a href="/wiki/1999_Rugby_World_Cup" title="1999 Rugby World Cup">1999</a>, <a href="/wiki/2003_Rugby_World_Cup" title="2003 Rugby World Cup">2003</a>, <a href="/wiki/2007_Rugby_World_Cup" title="2007 Rugby World Cup">2007</a>, <a href="/wiki/2011_Rugby_World_Cup" title="2011 Rugby World Cup">2011</a> and <a href="/wiki/2015_Rugby_World_Cup" title="2015 Rugby World Cup">2015</a> <a href="/wiki/Rugby_World_Cup" title="Rugby World Cup">Rugby World Cups</a>. <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">Cricket</a> is also popular, with the <a href="/wiki/Namibia_national_cricket_team" title="Namibia national cricket team">national side</a> having played in the <a href="/wiki/2003_Cricket_World_Cup" title="2003 Cricket World Cup">2003 Cricket World Cup</a>. In December 2017, Namibia Cricket reached the final of the Cricket South Africa (CSA) Provincial One Day Challenge for the first time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NCYR_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-NCYR-152">[152]</a></sup> In February 2018 Namibia hosted the ICC World Cricket League Division 2 with Namibia, Kenya, UAE, Nepal, Canada and Oman to compete for the final two ICC Cricket World Cup Qualifier positions in Zimbabwe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NCYR_152-1"><a href="#cite_note-NCYR-152">[152]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The most famous athlete from Namibia is <a href="/wiki/Frankie_Fredericks" title="Frankie Fredericks">Frankie Fredericks</a>, sprinter in the 100 and 200 m events. He won four Olympic silver medals (1992, 1996) and also has medals from several World Athletics Championships.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Golfer <a href="/wiki/Trevor_Dodds" title="Trevor Dodds">Trevor Dodds</a> won the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greater_Greensboro_Open" title="Greater Greensboro Open">Greater Greensboro Open</a> in 1998, one of 15 tournaments in his career. He achieved a career high world ranking of 78th in 1998.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Professional cyclist and Namibian Road Race champion <a href="/wiki/Dan_Craven" title="Dan Craven">Dan Craven</a> represented Namibia at the <a href="/wiki/2016_Summer_Olympics" title="2016 Summer Olympics">2016 Summer Olympics</a> in both the road race and individual time trial.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Boxer <a href="/wiki/Julius_Indongo" title="Julius Indongo">Julius Indongo</a> is the unified WBA, IBF, and IBO world champion in the <a href="/wiki/Light_welterweight" title="Light welterweight">Light welterweight</a> division.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Namibia" title="Media of Namibia">Media of Namibia</a></div>\n<p>Although Namibia\'s population is fairly small, the country has a diverse choice of media; two TV stations, 19 radio stations (without counting community stations), 5 daily newspapers, several weeklies and special publications compete for the attention of the audience. Additionally, a mentionable amount of foreign media, especially South African, is available. Online media are mostly based on print publication contents. Namibia has a state-owned Press Agency, called <a href="/wiki/Namibia_Press_Agency" title="Namibia Press Agency">NAMPA</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rothe_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rothe-153">[153]</a></sup> Overall <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr> 300 journalists work in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jobs_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-jobs-154">[154]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The first newspaper in Namibia was the German-language <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Windhoeker_Anzeiger&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Windhoeker Anzeiger (page does not exist)">Windhoeker Anzeiger</a></i>, founded 1898. During German rule, the newspapers mainly reflected the living reality and the view of the white German-speaking minority. The black majority was ignored or depicted as a threat. During South African rule, the white bias continued, with mentionable influence of the Pretoria government on the "South West African" media system. Independent newspapers were seen as a menace to the existing order, critical journalists threatened.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rothe_153-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rothe-153">[153]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Links_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-Links-156">[156]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Current daily newspapers are the private publications <i><a href="/wiki/The_Namibian" title="The Namibian">The Namibian</a></i> (English and other languages), <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Die_Republikein" title="Die Republikein">Die Republikein</a></i> (Afrikaans), <a href="/wiki/Allgemeine_Zeitung_(Namibia)" title="Allgemeine Zeitung (Namibia)">Allgemeine Zeitung</a> (German) and <i><a href="/wiki/Namibian_Sun" title="Namibian Sun">Namibian Sun</a></i> (English) as well as the state-owned <i><a href="/wiki/New_Era_(Namibia)" title="New Era (Namibia)">New Era</a></i> (predominantly English). Except for the largest newspaper, <i>The Namibian</i>, which is owned by a trust, the other mentioned private newspapers are part of the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Media_Holdings&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Democratic Media Holdings (page does not exist)">Democratic Media Holdings</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rothe_153-2"><a href="#cite_note-Rothe-153">[153]</a></sup> Other mentionable newspapers are the tabloid <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Informant%C3%A9&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Informant&#233; (page does not exist)">Informant&#233;</a></i> owned by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Trustco_Group_Holdings&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Trustco Group Holdings (page does not exist)">TrustCo</a>, the weekly <i><a href="/wiki/Windhoek_Observer" title="Windhoek Observer">Windhoek Observer</a></i>, the weekly <i><a href="/wiki/Namibia_Economist" title="Namibia Economist">Namibia Economist</a></i>, as well as the regional <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Namib_Times&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Namib Times (page does not exist)">Namib Times</a></i>. Current affairs magazines include <i><a href="/wiki/Insight_Namibia" title="Insight Namibia">Insight Namibia</a></i>, <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Vision2030_Focus_magazine&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Vision2030 Focus magazine (page does not exist)">Vision2030 Focus magazine</a></i><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> and <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Prime_FOCUS&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Prime FOCUS (page does not exist)">Prime FOCUS</a></i>. The <i><a href="/wiki/Sister_Namibia" title="Sister Namibia">Sister Namibia</a></i> magazine stands out as the longest running NGO magazine in Namibia, while <i><a href="/wiki/Namibia_Sport" title="Namibia Sport">Namibia Sport</a></i> is the only national sport magazine. Furthermore, the print market is complemented with party publications, student newspapers and PR publications.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rothe_153-3"><a href="#cite_note-Rothe-153">[153]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Radio was introduced in 1969, TV in 1981. The broadcasting sector today is dominated by the state-run <a href="/wiki/Namibian_Broadcasting_Corporation" title="Namibian Broadcasting Corporation">Namibian Broadcasting Corporation</a> (NBC). The <a href="/wiki/Public_broadcasting" title="Public broadcasting">public broadcaster</a> offers a TV station as well as a "National Radio" in English and nine language services in locally spoken languages. The nine private radio stations in the country are mainly English-language channels, except for Radio Omulunga (Oshiwambo) and Kosmos 94.1 (Afrikaans).\nPrivately held <a href="/wiki/One_Africa_Television" title="One Africa Television">One Africa TV</a> has competed with NBC since the 2000s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rothe_153-4"><a href="#cite_note-Rothe-153">[153]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oneafricabackground_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-oneafricabackground-157">[157]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Compared to neighbouring countries, Namibia has a large degree of media freedom. Over the past years, the country usually ranked in the upper quarter of the <a href="/wiki/Press_Freedom_Index" title="Press Freedom Index">Press Freedom Index</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reporters_without_Borders" title="Reporters without Borders">Reporters without Borders</a>, reaching position 21 in 2010, being on par with Canada and the best-positioned African country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=African_Media_Barometer&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="African Media Barometer (page does not exist)">African Media Barometer</a> shows similarly positive results.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> However, as in other countries, there is still mentionable influence of representatives of state and economy on media in Namibia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rothe_153-5"><a href="#cite_note-Rothe-153">[153]</a></sup> In 2009, Namibia dropped to position 36 on the Press Freedom Index.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> In 2013, it was 19th.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> In 2014 it ranked 22nd <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Media and journalists in Namibia are represented by the Namibian chapter of the <a href="/wiki/Media_Institute_of_Southern_Africa" title="Media Institute of Southern Africa">Media Institute of Southern Africa</a> and the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Editors%27_Forum_of_Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Editors\' Forum of Namibia (page does not exist)">Editors\' Forum of Namibia</a>. An independent media ombudsman was appointed in 2009 to prevent a state-controlled media council.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rothe_153-6"><a href="#cite_note-Rothe-153">[153]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:42817_06.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="434" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/42817_06.JPG/220px-42817_06.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/42817_06.JPG/330px-42817_06.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/42817_06.JPG/440px-42817_06.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:42817_06.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Secondary school students</div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Namibia" title="Education in Namibia">Education in Namibia</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_schools_in_Namibia" title="List of schools in Namibia">List of schools in Namibia</a></div>\n<p>Namibia has free education for both primary and secondary education levels. Grades 1&#8211;7 are primary level, grades 8&#8211;12 are secondary. In 1998, there were 400,325 Namibian students in primary school and 115,237 students in secondary schools. The pupil-teacher ratio in 1999 was estimated at 32:1, with about 8% of the GDP being spent on education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> Curriculum development, educational research, and professional development of teachers is centrally organised by the National Institute for Educational Development (NIED) in Okahandja.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Most schools in Namibia are state-run, but there are some private schools, which are also part of the country\'s education system. There are four teacher training universities, three colleges of agriculture, a police training college, and three universities: <a href="/wiki/University_of_Namibia" title="University of Namibia">University of Namibia</a> (UNAM), <a href="/wiki/International_University_of_Management" title="International University of Management">International University of Management</a> (IUM) and <a href="/wiki/Namibia_University_of_Science_and_Technology" title="Namibia University of Science and Technology">Namibia University of Science and Technology</a> (NUST).\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Namibia" title="Health in Namibia">Health in Namibia</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS_in_Namibia" title="HIV/AIDS in Namibia">HIV/AIDS in Namibia</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">Life expectancy</a> at birth is estimated to be 64 years in 2017&#160;&#8211; among the lowest in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Namibia launched a National Health Extension Programme in 2012<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> deployment 1,800 (2015) of a total ceiling of 4,800 health extension workers trained for six months in community health activities including first aid, health promotion for disease prevention, nutritional assessment and counseling, water sanitation and hygiene practices, HIV testing and community-based antiretroviral treatment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Namibia faces non-communicable disease burden. The Demographic and Health Survey (2013) summarizes findings on elevated blood pressure, hypertension, diabetes and obesity:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Among eligible respondents age 35&#8211;64, more than 4 in 10 women (44 percent) and men (45 percent) have elevated blood pressure or are currently taking medicine to lower their blood pressure.</li>\n<li>Forty-nine percent of women and 61 percent of men are not aware that they have elevated blood pressure.</li>\n<li>Forty-three percent of women and 34 percent of men with hypertension are taking medication for their condition.</li>\n<li>Only 29 percent of women and 20 percent of men with hypertension are taking medication and have their blood pressure under control.</li>\n<li>Six percent of women and 7 percent of men are diabetic; that is, they have elevated fasting plasma glucose values or report that they are taking diabetes medication. An additional 7 percent of women and 6 percent of men are prediabetic.</li>\n<li>Sixty-seven percent of women and 74 percent of men with diabetes are taking medication to lower their blood glucose.</li>\n<li>Women and men with a higher-than-normal body mass index (25.0 or higher) are more likely to have elevated blood pressure and elevated fasting blood glucose.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-:3-167">[167]</a></sup>&#160;</li></ul>\n<p>The HIV epidemic remains a public health issue in Namibia despite significant achievements made by the Ministry of Health and Social Services to expand HIV treatment services.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> In 2001, there were an estimated 210,000 people living with HIV/AIDS, and the estimated death toll in 2003 was 16,000. According to the 2011 UNAIDS Report, the epidemic in Namibia "appears to be leveling off."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> As the HIV/AIDS epidemic has reduced the working-aged population, the number of orphans has increased. It falls to the government to provide education, food, shelter and clothing for these orphans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> A Demographic and Health Survey with an HIV biomarker was completed in <a class="external text" href="https://dhsprogram.com/pubs/pdf/FR298/FR298.pdf" rel="nofollow">2013</a> and served as the fourth comprehensive, national-level population and health survey conducted in Namibia as part of the global Demographic and Health Surveys (DHS) programme. The DHS observed important characteristics associated to the HIV epidemic:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Overall, 26 percent of men age 15&#8211;49 and 32 percent of those age 50&#8211;64 have been circumcised.&#160;HIV prevalence for men age 15&#8211;49 is lower among circumcised (8.0 percent) than among uncircumcised men (11.9 percent). The pattern of lower HIV prevalence among circumcised than uncircumcised men is observed across most background characteristics. For each age group, circumcised men have lower HIV prevalence than those who are not circumcised; the difference is especially pronounced for men age 35&#8211;39 and 45&#8211;49 (11.7 percentage points each). The difference in HIV prevalence between uncircumcised and circumcised men is larger among urban than rural men (5.2 percentage points versus 2.1 percentage points).</li>\n<li>HIV prevalence among respondents age 15&#8211;49 is 16.9 percent for women and 10.9 percent for men. HIV prevalence rates among women and men age 50&#8211;64 are similar (16.7 percent and 16.0 percent, respectively).</li>\n<li>HIV prevalence peaks in the 35&#8211;39 age group for both women and men (30.9 percent and 22.6 percent, respectively). It is lowest among respondents age 15&#8211;24 (2.5&#8211;6.4 percent for women and 2.0&#8211;3.4 percent for men).</li>\n<li>Among respondents age 15&#8211;49, HIV prevalence is highest for women and men in Zambezi (30.9 percent and 15.9 percent, respectively) and lowest for women in Omaheke (6.9 percent) and men in Ohangwena (6.6 percent).</li>\n<li>In 76.4 percent of the 1,007 cohabiting couples who were tested for HIV in the 2013 NDHS, both partners were HIV negative; in 10.1 percent of the couples, both partners were HIV positive; and 13.5 percent of the couples were discordant (that is, one partner was infected with HIV and the other was not).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_167-1"><a href="#cite_note-:3-167">[167]</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p>As of 2015, the Ministry of Health and Social Services and UNAIDS produced a Progress <a class="external text" href="http://www.unaids.org/sites/default/files/country/documents/NAM_narrative_report_2015.pdf" rel="nofollow">Report</a> in which <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNAIDS" title="UNAIDS">UNAIDS</a> projected HIV prevalence among 15&#160;&#8211; 49 year olds at 13.3% [12.2%&#160;&#8211; 14.5%] and an estimated 210 000 [200 000&#160;&#8211; 230 000] living with HIV.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a> problem seems to be compounded by the AIDS epidemic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-172">[172]</a></sup> Research has shown that in Namibia the risk of contracting malaria is 14.5% greater if a person is also infected with HIV.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_172-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-172">[172]</a></sup> The risk of death from malaria is also raised by approximately 50% with a concurrent HIV infection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Korenromp_173-0"><a href="#cite_note-Korenromp-173">[173]</a></sup> The country had only 598 physicians in 2002.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" role="navigation" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">\n<ul style="display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold">\n<li style="display:table-row"><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center"><img alt="flag" class="noviewer thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" decoding="async" height="21" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Flag_of_Namibia.svg/48px-Flag_of_Namibia.svg.png 1.5x, Namibia-related articles">Index of Namibia-related articles</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Outline_of_Namibia" title="Outline of Namibia">Outline of Namibia</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Footnotes">Footnotes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Footnotes">edit</a><span The actual number of deaths in the limited number of battles with the Germany Schutztruppe (expeditionary force) were limited; most of the deaths occurred after fighting had ended. The German military governor <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Lotha_von_Trotha&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Lotha von Trotha (page does not exist)">Lotha von Trotha</a> issued an explicit extermination order, and many Herero died of disease and abuse in detention camps after being taken from their land. A substantial minority of Herero crossed the Kalahari desert into the British colony of Bechuanaland (modern-day <a href="/wiki/Botswana" title="Botswana">Botswana</a>), where a small community continues to live in western Botswana near to border with Namibia. <i>Let us die fighting</i>, originally published (1966) under the title <i>S&#252;dwestafrika unter deutsche Kolonialherrschaft</i>.
